## SECTION 4: SUPPORTING DOCUMENTS & FIELD REFERENCES

========== FILE: 03 - Reference Tools/Apex CompetitivePositioning.docx ==========
**APEX FOUNDATION SPECIALISTS**

**Competitive Positioning Reference**
=====================================

How to recognize a weaker scope and reframe the comparison in your
favor.

**How to Use This Reference**

This document is a field reference, not a sales script. When a customer
says they have a competing quote, do not attack the competitor. Ask to
see the proposal. Then use this reference to identify specific scope
gaps by name, explain what those gaps mean for the customer, and let the
evidence do the work.

**The most effective reframe is never "they're bad" --- it's "here's
what's in their proposal and here's what isn't." One missing line item
at a time.**

**1. The Competitor Landscape**

Who you're most likely competing against and how they typically operate

Apex competes most often in three tiers: national franchise operators,
regional waterproofing companies, and general contractors who
occasionally take foundation work. Each tier has predictable scope
patterns and predictable weaknesses.

  **COMPETITOR**                                        **THEIR TYPICAL SCOPE**                                                                                     **APEX ADVANTAGE**
  ----------------------------------------------------- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **NationalFranchises(e.g. BDry, TerraShield-type)**   Standardized install packages. Limited job-type flexibility. Franchise rep may be new to region.            Local expertise + regional soil and climate knowledge. No franchise upsell minimums. Scope built on evidence.
  **RegionalWaterproofers**                             Strong on drainage; weaker on encapsulation detail and wood assessment. May not offer poly or piers.        Full-scope capability across all five job types. One company for the complete system.
  **GeneralContractors**                                Often no dehumidifier sizing, no moisture meter documentation, no follow-up protocol. Sub the crawl work.   Specialized in foundation only. Not a side job. Evidence-based proposal and documented inspection.
  **DIY / HomeownerInstall Quotes**                     Big-box liner, no sealing at penetrations, no dehumidifier, no documentation. Customer does the labor.      Professional installation warranty. Proper dehumidifier sizing. Sealed penetrations. Documentation trail.

**2. Common Scope Gaps in Competitor Proposals**

What to look for when you ask to see their quote

When a customer shows you a competitor's proposal, read it the way a
building inspector would. The most valuable information is often what's
absent. The table below lists the gaps that appear most frequently and
how to recognize them in the document.

  **SCOPE GAP TO IDENTIFY**                                                                                                                                            **HOW YOU RECOGNIZE IT IN THE PROPOSAL**
  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **No dehumidifier (or undersized)**                                                                                                                                  Proposal lists liner and vent sealing with no dehumidifier. Or lists a unit with no model number or CFM rating --- cannot be verified.
  **Liner installed without drainage**                                                                                                                                 Proposal includes liner but no perimeter drain channel or sump. Ask the customer: is there active water staining or standing water?
  **No penetration sealing in scope**                                                                                                                                  Liner installation listed without "pipe and penetration sealing" as a separate line item. Penetrations are primary vapor entry points.
  **No moisture meter documentation**                                                                                                                                  No mention of moisture readings in the inspection report or proposal. No baseline = no warranty justification.
  **No wood treatment or remediation**                                                                                                                                 Elevated moisture present (from Apex inspection) but competitor proposal does not mention wood treatment, mold remediation, or joist repair.
  **Generic liner spec (no mil rating)**                                                                                                                               Proposal says "vapor barrier" with no mil thickness listed. 6-mil sheeting costs significantly less and performs worse than 12--20 mil.
  **No discharge endpoint specified**                                                                                                                                  Sump pump listed but no discharge pipe run in the scope. Where does the water go? Customer should ask this.
  **No follow-up or warranty terms**                                                                                                                                   Proposal has no post-installation follow-up process, no system check, and no written warranty with clear terms.
  **⚠ RULE:** Never tell the customer their other quote is wrong. Ask them questions that make the gap visible. The customer should reach the conclusion themselves.   

**3. Job-Type Specific Gaps**

What to probe by job type when competing against a lower quote

**Crawl Space Encapsulation**

The most competed job type. Also the one where scope differences are
most invisible to the customer. A 6-mil liner looks the same to a
homeowner as a 20-mil liner. The questions that expose the gap:

-   Does their quote include a dehumidifier? What model and CFM rating?

-   Does it include sealing all penetrations where pipes and wires pass
    > through the liner?

-   What mil thickness is the liner?

-   Is there documentation of moisture readings before and after?

-   What happens if moisture comes back? Is there a warranty and what
    > does it cover?

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **SCRIPT: Responding to a lower encapsulation quote**                |
|                                                                      |
| "I'd like to show you exactly what's in our proposal side by side    |
| with theirs. There are a few items that are easy to miss ---         |
| specifically the dehumidifier sizing and the penetration sealing.    |
| Can I walk you through those two line items?"                        |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

**Poly Injection / Slab Leveling**

Mudjacking is the most common low-cost alternative. It's heavier, less
precise, and requires larger holes. The customer often doesn't know the
difference.

-   Is the quote for mudjacking (slurry) or polyurethane foam? They are
    > not the same product.

-   Mudjacking material is heavy --- adds weight to already compromised
    > soil. Polyurethane is 2 lbs per cubic foot.

-   Mudjacking uses 2--3 inch holes. Poly injection uses 5/8 inch holes.
    > Ask the customer if appearance matters.

-   Does the quote identify the root cause of the settlement? Will the
    > repair last without addressing the cause?

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **SCRIPT: Mudjacking comparison**                                    |
|                                                                      |
| "There are two completely different products used for slab leveling  |
| --- mudjacking and polyurethane foam. I want to make sure you're     |
| comparing the same thing. Can I show you the difference in material  |
| weight and hole size?"                                               |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

**Structural Piers**

The most common competitive weakness here is pier count. A lower quote
often means fewer piers, which means each pier carries more load and the
system is more likely to fail unevenly.

-   How many piers are specified? Load per pier is critical to long-term
    > performance.

-   Is it push pier or helical pier? The footing condition determines
    > which is appropriate.

-   Is the lift guarantee documented in writing? What does
    > "stabilization" mean in their contract vs. ours?

-   Does the proposal include a post-installation elevation survey?

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **SCRIPT: Fewer piers in the competitor proposal**                   |
|                                                                      |
| "The most important number in a pier proposal isn't the price ---    |
| it's the pier count. Each pier carries a portion of the total load.  |
| Fewer piers means each one works harder. Can we look at the load     |
| distribution in both proposals?"                                     |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

**Crawl Space & Basement Drainage**

The most common gap here is an incomplete system: sump pump without a
perimeter drain channel, or encapsulation over an active water source.

-   Does the proposal include a perimeter drain channel connecting to
    > the sump? A pump alone does not capture water at the wall-floor
    > joint.

-   Is the sump pump connected to a properly sloped discharge line with
    > a confirmed exit point?

-   If there's a liner in their scope, is drainage installed first?
    > Liner over standing water is a callback waiting to happen.

-   Is a battery backup specified? Power outages happen during the
    > storms that cause flooding.

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **SCRIPT: Sump pump only vs. full drainage system**                  |
|                                                                      |
| "A sump pump on its own only removes water that pools at the lowest  |
| point of the floor. The water entering at your wall-floor joint goes |
| around it. A perimeter drain channel is what connects those entry    |
| points to the pump. Does their proposal show a channel?"             |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

**4. The Rules of Competitive Conversations**

Non-negotiable conduct standards when a customer has another quote

  **NEVER DO THIS**                                        **DO THIS INSTEAD**
  -------------------------------------------------------- -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  Say "they're a bad company" or attack their reputation   Let the proposal speak. Name what's missing, not who's wrong.
  Guess at what's in their proposal                        Ask to see it. Read it. Use this reference. Don't speculate.
  Drop your price to match theirs                          Add value. Explain what's included and why. Price-matching a lesser scope is a race to the bottom.
  Tell the customer they're making a mistake               Ask questions. Let the customer identify the concern themselves. Pushed customers don't close.
  Dismiss the competitor's company size or experience      Stay on scope and documentation. Technical gaps close sales. Personal attacks alienate customers.
  Panic if the price difference is large                   A \$3,000 gap on a crawl space is \$250/year over 12 years. Frame it against the home's value and lifespan.

**5. The Universal Reframe**

Works in any competitive situation when the customer shows you a lower
quote

When a customer presents a lower quote, the goal of the reframe is not
to win an argument. It's to change the question the customer is asking
from "why does Apex cost more?" to "what does the other proposal not
include?" These are fundamentally different conversations.

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **SCRIPT: Opening a competitive comparison --- any job type**        |
|                                                                      |
| "I appreciate you being transparent with me about the other quote.   |
| I'd actually love to look at it with you. In my experience, when     |
| there's a significant price difference, it's almost always because   |
| of specific items that are in one proposal and not the other. Can we |
| go through both together?"                                           |
+======================================================================+
| **SCRIPT: Closing the comparison after identifying gaps**            |
|                                                                      |
| "So the price difference between the two proposals is about \$X.     |
| What we've found is that \[specific gap 1\] and \[specific gap 2\]   |
| aren't in their scope. If you had to add those back in, you'd be     |
| paying for them separately anyway --- and probably not under         |
| warranty. Does that change how you see the comparison?"              |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **SCRIPT: When the customer still leans toward the lower quote**     |
|                                                                      |
| "I completely understand --- price is real and it matters. I'm not   |
| here to tell you what to do. What I'd ask is that before you make    |
| your decision, you get in writing from the other company exactly     |
| what \[specific gap\] covers. If they put it in writing with the     |
| same scope, they've earned the job."                                 |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

**6. Financing as a Competitive Tool**

Most competitors don't lead with financing. You should.

A \$5,200 Apex proposal against a \$3,800 competitor proposal looks like
a \$1,400 problem. At a 12-month same-as-cash rate, it's a \$117/month
difference. Most competitors who price lower are also less likely to
offer flexible financing. Lead with the monthly comparison, not the
total.

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **SCRIPT: Converting the price objection to a financing              |
| conversation**                                                       |
|                                                                      |
| "Let me show you what the monthly difference actually looks like. On |
| a 12-month same-as-cash, the difference between the two proposals is |
| about \$\[X\]/month. And our proposal includes \[specific items not  |
| in competitor quote\]. Would that change the math for you?"          |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

Upgrade and GoodLeap both offer 12-month same-as-cash options. Know
these programs cold. A rep who can run the financing number on the spot
wins the comparison before the customer leaves the table.

========== FILE: 03 - Reference Tools/Apex InspectionChecklists.docx ==========
**APEX FOUNDATION SPECIALISTS**

**Field Inspection Checklists**

Use during every appointment --- documentation before proposal

Checklist 1 --- Crawl Space Encapsulation

Checklist 2 --- Poly Injection / Slab Leveling

Checklist 3 --- Structural Piers

Checklist 4 --- Crawl Space Drainage

Checklist 5 --- Basement Drainage

Internal Use Only

**How to Use These Checklists**
===============================

These checklists are active tools, not study materials. Work through
them during every appointment. The proposal you build should be
traceable, line by line, to something you checked off or measured here.

Each checklist has four phases: pre-inspection (site and history before
entering the space), inspection (measurements, photos, and conditions),
required photos (the non-negotiable documentation for every appointment
of this type), and diagnostic flags (conditions that change the
recommendation if present and must be evaluated before leaving the
space).

  ⚠   **Red rows are critical flags** that change what you recommend. Never proceed without evaluating these.
  --- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  ★   **Orange-accented rows are required** on every appointment of this type.
  ☐   **Standard rows** document conditions present in this specific appointment.

The green Inspection Summary box at the bottom of each checklist is
filled in before you sit down with the customer. It documents your
overall assessment while findings are fresh.

**CHECKLIST 1 --- CRAWL SPACE**

**Encapsulation Inspection**
============================

Complete before building any encapsulation proposal

  --------------------------------------------------- ---------------------------------- ---------------------------------- -----------------------------------

**Phase 1 --- Pre-Inspection**
------------------------------

+-------------------+-------------------------------------------------+
| **SITE & ACCESS** |                                                 |
+===================+=================================================+
| ☐                 | Confirm crawl space access point and clear path |
|                   | for entry                                       |
+-------------------+-------------------------------------------------+
| ☐                 | Photograph exterior of home and grading around  |
|                   | foundation                                      |
+-------------------+-------------------------------------------------+
| ☐                 | Note any downspouts or gutters discharging near |
|                   | the foundation                                  |
|                   |                                                 |
|                   | Water directed at the foundation is often the   |
|                   | cause of the problem                            |
+-------------------+-------------------------------------------------+
| ☐                 | Note large trees within 15--20 feet of the      |
|                   | crawl space                                     |
|                   |                                                 |
|                   | Root desiccation can contribute to seasonal     |
|                   | moisture variation                              |
+-------------------+-------------------------------------------------+
| ☐                 | Confirm customer's primary concern before       |
|                   | beginning                                       |
|                   |                                                 |
|                   | Ask: 'Is there anything specific you want me to |
|                   | make sure I look at?'                           |
+-------------------+-------------------------------------------------+

**Phase 2 --- Crawl Space Inspection**
--------------------------------------

+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **MOISTURE           |                      |                      |
| MEASUREMENTS (record |                      |                      |
| in table below)**    |                      |                      |
+======================+======================+======================+
| ☐                    | Take moisture meter  |                      |
|                      | reading on sill      |                      |
|                      | plate (lowest wood   |                      |
|                      | member)              |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | Normal: 12--15% \|   |                      |
|                      | Elevated: 19%+ \|    |                      |
|                      | Active rot           |                      |
|                      | threshold: 28%+      |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Take moisture meter  |                      |
|                      | reading on floor     |                      |
|                      | joists in at least 3 |                      |
|                      | locations            |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | Photograph each      |                      |
|                      | reading with the     |                      |
|                      | meter visible in the |                      |
|                      | frame                |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Take relative        |                      |
|                      | humidity reading in  |                      |
|                      | the crawl space      |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | Safe below 60% \|    |                      |
|                      | Mold cannot sustain  |                      |
|                      | growth below 60% \|  |                      |
|                      | Problem above 60%    |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Note any visible     |                      |
|                      | condensation on      |                      |
|                      | surfaces             |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **MEASUREMENT**      | **RECORDED VALUE**   | **REFERENCE /        |
|                      |                      | THRESHOLD**          |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **Sill plate MC**    | \_\_                 | Normal 12--15% /     |
|                      | \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ | Elevated 19%+ / Rot  |
|                      |                      | threshold 28%+       |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **Floor joist MC --- | \_\_                 | Normal 12--15% /     |
| location 1**         | \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ | Elevated 19%+ / Rot  |
|                      |                      | threshold 28%+       |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **Floor joist MC --- | \_\_                 | Normal 12--15% /     |
| location 2**         | \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ | Elevated 19%+ / Rot  |
|                      |                      | threshold 28%+       |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **Floor joist MC --- | \_\_                 | Normal 12--15% /     |
| location 3**         | \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ | Elevated 19%+ / Rot  |
|                      |                      | threshold 28%+       |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **Crawl space RH**   | \_\_                 | Safe below 60% /     |
|                      | \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ | Mold-sustaining      |
|                      |                      | above 60%            |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **Crawl space sq ft  | \_\_                 | For dehumidifier     |
| (approx)**           | \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ | sizing               |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **STRUCTURAL &       |                      |                      |
| MOISTURE             |                      |                      |
| CONDITIONS**         |                      |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Inspect all exposed  |                      |
|                      | wood for visible     |                      |
|                      | mold or              |                      |
|                      | discoloration        |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | Photograph any       |                      |
|                      | affected areas       |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Inspect sill plate   |                      |
|                      | for rot, softness,   |                      |
|                      | or pest damage       |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | Check with moisture  |                      |
|                      | meter and probe if   |                      |
|                      | uncertain            |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Inspect floor joists |                      |
|                      | for sag, cracks, or  |                      |
|                      | deterioration        |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Inspect existing     |                      |
|                      | insulation condition |                      |
|                      | if present           |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | Wet, sagging, or     |                      |
|                      | molded fiberglass    |                      |
|                      | batts must be        |                      |
|                      | removed as part of   |                      |
|                      | scope                |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | **Check for standing |                      |
|                      | water or active      |                      |
|                      | water staining on    |                      |
|                      | soil**               |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | Water staining =     |                      |
|                      | bulk water entry --- |                      |
|                      | drainage may be      |                      |
|                      | required before      |                      |
|                      | encapsulation        |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Check for            |                      |
|                      | efflorescence on     |                      |
|                      | block piers or       |                      |
|                      | foundation walls     |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | White mineral        |                      |
|                      | deposits = evidence  |                      |
|                      | of recurring water   |                      |
|                      | movement through     |                      |
|                      | wall                 |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Check for pest       |                      |
|                      | activity: termite    |                      |
|                      | tubes, rodent        |                      |
|                      | nesting, insect      |                      |
|                      | damage               |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Inspect any existing |                      |
|                      | liner: age,          |                      |
|                      | coverage, seal       |                      |
|                      | integrity, and       |                      |
|                      | condition            |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Check all crawl      |                      |
|                      | space vents: open,   |                      |
|                      | closed, screened, or |                      |
|                      | blocked              |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Check crawl space    |                      |
|                      | access door: sealed, |                      |
|                      | unsealed, or missing |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| ☐                    | Inspect any existing |                      |
|                      | sump pump or         |                      |
|                      | dehumidifier         |                      |
|                      |                      |                      |
|                      | Note model, age if   |                      |
|                      | visible, operational |                      |
|                      | status               |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+
| **⚠ CRITICAL FLAG:** |                      |                      |
| If standing water or |                      |                      |
| active water         |                      |                      |
| staining is present, |                      |                      |
| evaluate whether     |                      |                      |
| drainage must be     |                      |                      |
| installed before     |                      |                      |
| encapsulation.       |                      |                      |
| Installing a liner   |                      |                      |
| over an active bulk  |                      |                      |
| water source traps   |                      |                      |
| water beneath it and |                      |                      |
| produces conditions  |                      |                      |
| worse than the       |                      |                      |
| unsealed crawl       |                      |                      |
| space.               |                      |                      |
+----------------------+----------------------+----------------------+

**Phase 3 --- Required Photos**
-------------------------------

  **✓**   **PHOTO SUBJECT**                                              **STATUS**
  ------- -------------------------------------------------------------- --------------
  ☐       **Moisture meter on sill plate (meter visible in frame)**      **REQUIRED**
  ☐       **Moisture meter on floor joist (meter visible in frame)**     **REQUIRED**
  ☐       **Overall crawl space from access point**                      **REQUIRED**
  ☐       **Any visible mold or discoloration on wood**                  **REQUIRED**
  ☐       **Any water staining on soil, walls, or piers**                **REQUIRED**
  ☐       Condition of any existing liner (especially edges and seams)   if present
  ☐       Crawl space vents and access door condition                    if present
  ☐       Any pest damage, termite tubes, or rodent activity             if present
  ☐       Exterior grading and downspout discharge locations             if present

**Phase 4 --- Diagnostic Flags**
--------------------------------

+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| **EVALUATE BEFORE LEAVING THE    |                                  |
| CRAWL SPACE**                    |                                  |
+==================================+==================================+
| ☐                                | **Is bulk water entry present?   |
|                                  | (standing water, active          |
|                                  | staining, efflorescence)**       |
|                                  |                                  |
|                                  | YES = drainage must precede      |
|                                  | encapsulation --- document in    |
|                                  | proposal                         |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| ☐                                | Is existing insulation present   |
|                                  | in joist bays?                   |
|                                  |                                  |
|                                  | YES = removal is required as     |
|                                  | part of scope                    |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| ☐                                | Are there unsealed plumbing      |
|                                  | penetrations in the liner zone?  |
|                                  |                                  |
|                                  | Must be included in sealing      |
|                                  | scope                            |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| ☐                                | Is sq footage accurately         |
|                                  | estimated for dehumidifier       |
|                                  | sizing?                          |
|                                  |                                  |
|                                  | Undersized dehumidifier produces |
|                                  | continuous cycling and early     |
|                                  | failure                          |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| ☐                                | **Is active pest activity        |
|                                  | present that requires treatment  |
|                                  | before sealing?**                |
|                                  |                                  |
|                                  | Sealing before treating traps    |
|                                  | pests inside the system          |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| **INSPECTION SUMMARY**           |                                  |
|                                  |                                  |
| Primary moisture issue: vapor    |                                  |
| only / bulk water + vapor / bulk |                                  |
| water only                       |                                  |
|                                  |                                  |
| Highest MC reading:              |                                  |
| \_\_\_\_\_\_\_%   Average RH:    |                                  |
| \_\_\_\_\_\_\_%                  |                                  |
|                                  |                                  |
| Existing liner present: yes / no |                                  |
|   Dehumidifier present: yes / no |                                  |
|                                  |                                  |
| Drainage required before         |                                  |
| encapsulation: yes / no          |                                  |
|                                  |                                  |
| Scope recommendation:            |                                  |
| \_\_\_                           |                                  |
| \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ |                                  |
| \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ |                                  |
| \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ |                                  |
