========== FILE: 03 - Reference Tools/Apex_SalesFieldGuide.docx ==========
**APEX FOUNDATION SPECIALISTS**

**Sales Field Guide**

The Complete Rep Reference for the Florida Panhandle & South Alabama

**What's Inside**

Part 1 --- The Sales Process (Pre-Inspection through Follow-Up)

Part 2 --- Customer Psychology (How Decisions Are Made)

Part 3 --- Job Type Reference (All 5 Job Types)

Part 4 --- Objection Handling (16 Objections, 5 Categories)

Part 5 --- Key Numbers & Scripts (Quick-Reference)

Internal Training Use Only --- Not for Distribution

**How to Use This Guide**
=========================

This guide is the portable reference version of the complete Apex sales
and product curriculum. Everything in here comes from the full training
deck series --- the six-module Sales Process Curriculum, the Customer
Psychology module, the five Job Type Education decks, and the Objection
Handling reference. The goal was to give you one document you can study
before your first appointment, read cover to cover when you're getting
started, and flip back to in the field when you need a quick reminder.

The guide is organized in the same sequence as the curriculum. Part 1
walks through the full appointment process from pre-inspection to
post-appointment follow-up. Part 2 covers the psychology of how
customers make decisions, which is the framework behind everything in
Parts 3 and 4. Part 3 is your job type reference --- a tight summary of
each of the five products Apex installs, covering the problem, the
cause, the right repair, the key technical specs, and the most important
things to say and avoid. Part 4 is the objection handling reference.
Part 5 collects all the key numbers, thresholds, and model scripts in
one place.

  -- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **HOW TO STUDY:** Read Part 1 and Part 2 once through before your first ride-along. Before each appointment, flip to the relevant Job Type section in Part 3 and review the "In the Field" entries. Keep the Objection Reference in Part 4 open on your phone.
  -- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**PART 1**

**The Sales Process**
=====================

Every Apex appointment follows the same five-phase structure. The phases
are sequential, and skipping or rushing any of them tends to show up
later --- usually as an objection you could have prevented or a close
you lose because trust wasn't built early enough. The structure is not a
script. It's a framework that gives you consistency without making you
sound like you're reading from a card.

**Phase 1 --- Pre-Inspection: Setting Up the Appointment**
----------------------------------------------------------

Most of the close happens before you ever walk in the door. The
pre-inspection phase exists to establish rapport, reduce cancellations,
and make sure the customer is mentally ready to have a real conversation
when you arrive --- not just when they see the invoice.

### **The 2-Day-Out Call**

Call the customer 48 hours before the appointment. Keep it brief. The
goal is to confirm, build a small amount of anticipation, and make sure
nothing has changed. A customer who hears your voice before they see
your face is already warming up.

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **2-Day-Out Script**                                                 |
|                                                                      |
| "Hi \[Name\], this is \[Your Name\] from Apex Foundation             |
| Specialists. I'm calling to confirm your inspection scheduled for    |
| \[Day\] at \[Time\]. I've already reviewed what you shared with us   |
| and I'm looking forward to coming out. Is there anything specific    |
| you want me to make sure I look at?"                                 |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

That last question is important. It gives the customer a sense of
control and often surfaces the concern they're most worried about, which
tells you a great deal about what kind of close this appointment is
likely to need.

### **The 30-Minute-Out Call**

Call when you're 30 minutes away. This is a courtesy call, but it does
something more important: it puts a human moment right before you
arrive. A customer who just heard your voice is much more likely to be
at the door ready to meet you than one who hears a random knock.

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **30-Minute-Out Script**                                             |
|                                                                      |
| "Hi \[Name\], it's \[Your Name\] from Apex --- just wanted to give   |
| you a heads-up that I'm about 30 minutes out. Looking forward to     |
| seeing you shortly."                                                 |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

**Phase 2 --- The Inspection**
------------------------------

The inspection phase is where your credibility is built or lost. Every
measurement you take, every photo you document, every observation you
explain out loud is evidence. The customer who watches a rep who clearly
knows what they're doing --- who names the crack pattern, reads the
moisture meter, and explains what the numbers mean --- experiences
something very different from the customer who watches a rep walk around
taking pictures without saying anything.

### **The Customer Walk-Around**

Start outside with the customer present. Walk the perimeter and explain
what you're looking at. You don't need to diagnose yet --- just observe
out loud. "I want to look at the grading here because the way water
moves around the foundation affects what's happening below." This
establishes that your inspection is systematic, not a sales routine.

### **The Full Inspection**

Go into the crawl space or basement alone. Take photos of everything
noteworthy. Use the moisture meter on multiple wood members and document
the readings. Look for water staining, efflorescence, mold, structural
damage, pest activity, and the condition of any existing systems
(liners, sump pumps, prior repairs). The photos and readings are your
proposal's foundation --- without them you are asking the customer to
trust your word rather than their own eyes.

  -- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **KEY PRINCIPLE:** Every recommendation in your proposal should be traceable to something you documented during the inspection. If you cannot point to the photo or reading that justifies a line item, that line item will be challenged.
  -- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **The Post-Inspection Door Knock**

When you come out of the crawl space, pause before presenting. Wash up,
take a breath, and organize your thoughts for 90 seconds. Then knock and
ask for the kitchen table. The transition from inspection to
presentation is itself a signal: you found things worth sitting down and
discussing.

### **The 15-Minute Window**

You have approximately 15 minutes after coming out of the crawl space
before the customer's attention and receptivity begin to fade. Don't
spend that window building the proposal on your tablet. Spend it
reviewing photos with the customer. The presentation builds itself out
of the photos. The photos are what make the proposal feel like a
diagnosis rather than a sales pitch.

**Phase 3 --- The Presentation**
--------------------------------

The presentation phase is the education phase. You are not pitching. You
are explaining what you found, why it matters, and what the correct
approach is. The sequence that works is always: problem first, then
cause, then what doesn't work, then the right repair. That sequence
mirrors the way the job type decks are structured, and it mirrors the
way human beings process new information.

### **Photo Review**

Start every presentation by reviewing the photos with the customer, not
by opening the proposal. "Let me show you what I found." Each
significant photo gets a plain-language explanation: what it is, what
caused it, and what it means if left unaddressed. The photos create
shared context. The proposal then fills in the solution to a problem the
customer has now seen with their own eyes.

### **The Education Phase**

After the photos, explain the problem in the cascade format: what is
happening mechanically, why it's happening, and what the progression
looks like over time. You are not trying to scare the customer. You are
giving them accurate information about where they are on a progression
curve. The customer who understands the mechanism is far more likely to
act than the customer who just heard that there's a problem.

### **Wrong Fixes**

Before presenting your repair recommendation, briefly address the
alternatives the customer is likely considering. Not to dismiss them,
but to explain accurately why each one is incomplete for their specific
conditions. A customer who understands why the cheaper option doesn't
solve their specific problem doesn't feel pressured into the more
complete solution --- they feel informed.

### **Building the Proposal**

Build the proposal in front of the customer, not before the appointment
and not after you've left. Walk through each component, explain what it
does, and say what happens if that component is not included. The
customer who understands their proposal is far more likely to sign it
and far less likely to cancel it later.

### **Financing Framing**

Introduce financing before you present the total price. "We have two
financing options --- Upgrade and GoodLeap --- and I'll show you both. A
lot of customers find that the monthly payment is a lot more manageable
than the lump sum." This reframes the price conversation before it
starts.

### **The First Ask**

After building the proposal and walking through the numbers, ask for the
decision. Not aggressively, not apologetically. Confidently. "Based on
everything I documented today, I'd like to get this scheduled for you.
Does this work?" If the customer says yes, you're done. If they have
questions or objections, you're in Phase 4.

**Phase 4 --- The Close**
-------------------------

The close phase is not a manipulation phase. It is a conversation phase.
A customer who is still at the table after Phase 3 has not said no ---
they have said not yet. Your job is to understand what "not yet" means
for this specific customer and address it specifically.

### **Objection Handling**

See Part 4 of this guide for the complete objection reference. The core
principle applies to all of them: every objection is a request for more
information, more evidence, or more reassurance. The customer who says
"it's too expensive" is asking you to help them see the value. The
customer who says "I need to think about it" is asking you to find out
what specifically still concerns them. The customer who says "my
neighbor said it wasn't serious" is asking you to give them something to
replace that impression with.

### **Right-Sizing**

If the full scope is genuinely not viable for the customer right now,
identify the minimum complete system --- the smallest scope that
actually solves the problem without creating new ones --- and offer
that. Never reduce scope without explaining the trade-off in writing.
Never propose a partial system and call it a solution.

### **The Second Ask**

After addressing the primary objection, ask again. Not identically ---
with the updated information incorporated. "Given what I've explained
about the moisture cascade, does it make sense to get this on the
schedule?" If you get a second objection, address it and ask again. Most
closes happen on the second or third ask when everything else has been
done right.

  -- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **REMEMBER:** The customer who objects twice and then agrees is not a customer you pressured. They are a customer you informed twice.
  -- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Phase 5 --- Post-Appointment Follow-Up**
------------------------------------------

The appointment ends when the customer signs or explicitly declines.
Everything after that is the follow-up phase --- and it is where most of
the jobs that should close eventually do close, if the rep follows up
correctly.

### **The 5-Touch Follow-Up System**

  **Touch 1**   Same day --- send the documentation and a brief message confirming what you discussed.
  ------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Touch 2**   48 hours --- check in with a specific question, not a generic "following up."
  **Touch 3**   1 week --- a value-add message. Share something relevant to their specific situation.
  **Touch 4**   2--3 weeks --- persistence without pressure. Acknowledge the timing and keep the door open.
  **Touch 5**   6 weeks --- final follow-up. Frame it as a completion. After this, move to low-frequency monitoring.

### **Referral Capture**

The best time to ask for a referral is right after a positive moment ---
immediately after signing, or during any follow-up call where the
customer expresses satisfaction. "I really appreciate the kind words. If
you know anyone else dealing with similar issues, I'd be grateful if
you'd pass along my name." That's the whole script. The research is
clear: a personal referral from a trusted peer converts at rates
dramatically higher than any cold lead.

**PART 2**

**Customer Psychology**
=======================

Understanding how customers make decisions is not a manipulation skill
--- it is an empathy skill. The rep who knows how decisions are actually
made is better equipped to give each customer the specific information
they need to feel confident, because that rep understands what kind of
information matters most to each type of person.

**How Decisions Are Actually Made**
-----------------------------------

Behavioral research has consistently demonstrated that most major
purchase decisions are made emotionally first and justified rationally
afterward. This is not a weakness in the customer --- it is how human
decision-making works. The emotional centers of the brain process
potential threats and benefits faster than the analytical centers can
evaluate evidence. A customer who feels that a problem is genuinely
threatening to something they care about --- their home, their family's
health, their financial security --- will find reasons to act. A
customer who doesn't feel that emotional connection will find reasons to
wait, regardless of how complete the evidence is.

This means your job is not only to present evidence but to connect
evidence to what the customer actually cares about. The same moisture
reading means something completely different to a customer who is
terrified about mold affecting her asthmatic child than it does to a
customer whose primary concern is what happens to his home's value when
he sells in three years. Same evidence. Different frames. Different
closes.

  -- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **CORE PRINCIPLE:** People buy outcomes, not products. They buy a dry basement, not a drainage system. They buy a stable foundation, not piers. Connect the product to the outcome the customer cares about.
  -- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Loss Aversion**
-----------------

The most powerful psychological force in home improvement sales is loss
aversion: the well-documented human tendency to feel the pain of a
potential loss more acutely than the pleasure of an equivalent gain.
Research by behavioral economists Kahneman and Tversky demonstrated that
the psychological impact of a loss is roughly twice the impact of an
equivalent gain. In practical terms: a customer will work harder to
avoid losing \$5,000 in home equity than they will to gain \$5,000 in
home value.

This is why the most effective urgency framing in foundation repair is
not "here's what you'll gain" --- it is "here's what you're at risk of
losing." The risk of progressive structural damage, the risk of a home
inspection flagging an unresolved problem before a sale, the risk of
secondary repairs that become necessary if the primary issue is not
addressed --- these are all loss frames, and they are legitimately
accurate. Evidence-based urgency using loss framing is not manipulation.
It is giving the customer the complete picture.

  -- -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **⚠ AVOID:** Never manufacture urgency. If the inspection doesn't support urgency, don't invent it. Customers can sense fabricated pressure, and it destroys trust permanently. Evidence-based urgency from specific findings closes jobs. Generic pressure loses them.
  -- -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**The Four Emotional Drivers**
------------------------------

Customers come to foundation repair appointments with one of four
primary emotional drivers. Identifying which driver is operating for a
specific customer --- usually from the way they describe the problem and
the questions they ask in the first five minutes --- allows you to frame
the repair around what they actually care about.

  **Fear & Loss Aversion**   Worried the problem is getting worse. Asks what happens if nothing is done. Responds to specific progression mechanisms and documented severity.
  -------------------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Protection & Safety**    Concerned about family health, structural safety, or occupant wellbeing. Often has children, elderly relatives, or health-sensitive family members. Responds to air quality data and structural risk framing.
  **Financial & Equity**     Focused on home value, resale implications, and ROI. Asks about warranty transferability and inspection report implications. Responds to cost-of-inaction and equity protection framing.
  **Pride & Quality**        Wants the problem resolved correctly, completely, and permanently. Skeptical of shortcuts. Responds to technical depth, complete system explanations, and the contrast between half-measures and full solutions.

**Reading the Room**
--------------------

Most customers signal their primary driver within the first few minutes
of the appointment. Pay attention to the first question they ask when
you arrive. Pay attention to what they show you first. Pay attention to
what they emphasize when they describe the problem. A customer who leads
with "I'm worried about what this is doing to my floors upstairs" is
showing a safety/protection driver. A customer who leads with "I'm
planning to sell in two years" is showing a financial/equity driver.
Once you've identified the driver, make sure your presentation connects
the technical findings to that specific concern.

  -- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **FIELD TIP:** If you're unsure which driver is operating, ask a simple question early: 'What concerns you most about this situation?' The answer is almost always a direct statement of the emotional driver.
  -- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**The Four Buyer Personalities**
--------------------------------

  **The Analytical**            Has done research. Asks technical questions. Skeptical of claims without evidence. Wants specifics. Responds best to: data-first presentations, honest comparisons, technical depth from the job type sections of this guide.
  ----------------------------- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **The Skeptic**               Has been burned before or is generally distrustful of contractors. May be guarded or even slightly hostile early. Responds best to: validation of prior experiences, specific explanations of what makes this different, referral book and local social proof.
  **The Decisive**              Wants to make a decision efficiently. Values clarity and confidence over exhaustive explanation. Responds best to: a clear recommendation with a clear rationale. Don't over-explain --- they'll ask if they want more.
  **The Relationship-Driven**   Makes decisions based on trust and personal connection. Values being heard and understood. Responds best to: genuine listening early in the appointment, empathy for the inconvenience the problem has caused, personal references from neighbors.

**PART 3**

**Job Type Reference**
======================

This section is your pre-appointment study guide for each of the five
job types Apex installs. For each job type you'll find the problem
defined, the cause explained, the key technical specs you need to know
cold, and the most important things to say and avoid in the field. Read
the full job type training decks for the complete technical depth. Use
this section as your fast review before appointments.

**JOB TYPE 1**

**Crawl Space Encapsulation**
-----------------------------

Encapsulation is the complete sealing of the crawl space from the
outside environment --- isolating it from ground moisture, outdoor
humidity, outside air, and pests --- so that the space below the home
behaves like a controlled part of the building rather than an extension
of the outdoors.

### **The Problem: The Moisture Cascade**

Moisture damage in a crawl space is not a single event --- it is a
cascade. Up to 10--15 gallons of water evaporates daily from exposed
crawl space soil. That moisture raises relative humidity to 80--100% in
summer. When humid air contacts cooler wood surfaces, it condenses,
raising wood moisture content. Above 19%, wood is at elevated risk.
Above 28%, wood-decay fungi become active. Mold colonizes wood under
sustained high humidity. The stack effect then draws mold spores,
allergens, and moisture upward into the first-floor living space:
40--50% of the air in the first floor of a crawl-space home comes from
the crawl space below it.

### **Why the Panhandle Is High-Risk**

Average summer relative humidity exceeds 80%. Sandy coastal soils have
limited capillary resistance, meaning ground moisture migrates readily
upward. Temperatures rarely drop cold enough to interrupt mold growth
cycles. Traditional venting --- which was the building standard for
decades --- actually makes moisture problems worse in hot-humid
climates: warm outdoor air entering a cooler crawl space condenses
immediately, depositing its moisture load on every surface.

### **Key Technical Specs**

  **Liner thickness**    20-mil minimum (6-mil and 10-mil alternatives tear under foot traffic within 2--3 years)
  ---------------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Normal wood MC**     12--15% (equilibrium moisture content in a dry environment)
  **Elevated wood MC**   19%+ (risk zone --- document with moisture meter photos)
  **Rot threshold**      28%+ (active wood-decay fungi can establish)
  **Safe RH target**     Below 60% (below 55% preferred --- mold cannot sustain growth below 60%)
  **Soil evaporation**   10--15 gallons per day from exposed soil in a typical crawl space
  **Air exchange**       40--50% of first-floor air comes from the crawl space via the stack effect
  **Energy savings**     Homes with sealed crawl spaces average 15%+ reduction in HVAC costs
  **Dehumidifier**       Commercial-grade only --- rated 40°F--100°F, auto-drain, digital humidistat

### **In the Field: What to Say**

On urgency: Connect the moisture reading to the specific thresholds
above.

+----------------------------------------------------------------------+
| **Example**                                                          |
|                                                                      |
| "The reading I'm showing you here is 24%. Normal is 12--15%. Above   |
| 28%, wood-decay fungi become active. You're already in a range where |
| the conditions for rot are present --- we're not there yet, but the  |
| conditions that produced this reading will continue producing it     |
| every wet season."                                                   |
+----------------------------------------------------------------------+

On the system: Explain each component's role, especially the
dehumidifier.

\'A liner without a dehumidifier is like putting a tarp on a wet floor
without fixing the leak. The liner reduces ground vapor, but humid air
continues to enter through every unsealed vent and gap. The dehumidifier
is what gives the sealed space humidity control.\'

  -- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **⚠ AVOID:** Do not install encapsulation without evaluating for bulk water entry. If water is actively entering the space, drainage must go in first. A liner installed over an active water source traps water beneath it and produces conditions worse than the unsealed crawl space.
  -- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**JOB TYPE 2**

**Poly Injection / Slab Leveling**
----------------------------------

Polyurethane injection leveling is the process of lifting a sunken
concrete slab back to grade by injecting a high-density two-part
expanding foam beneath it --- filling the voids that caused the settling
and restoring the soil's load-bearing capacity without tearing out the
existing concrete.

### **Why Slabs Sink**

Concrete doesn't fail --- the soil beneath it does. The five most common
causes in this region: (1) water erosion washing fine soil particles out
from under the slab over time; (2) poor compaction at construction ---
fill soil that was never properly compacted, settling over 5--10 years;
(3) shrink-swell clay soil cycles under seasonal moisture variation; (4)
plumbing leaks continuously saturating and eroding the soil beneath the
slab; (5) organic decay or pest activity creating voids beneath the
concrete. Always identify the likely cause during the inspection and
address it in the proposal --- a lifted slab over an unresolved cause
will settle again.

  -- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **CRITICAL:** If the settlement is localized, rapid, or follows a linear path (suggesting a pipe route), evaluate for a plumbing leak before recommending injection. Injecting foam over an active plumbing leak produces temporary results and may mask a worsening structural problem.
  -- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **Key Technical Specs**

  **Hole diameter**       5/8" (approximately the size of a dime vs. 2"--2.5" for mudjacking)
  ----------------------- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Foam expansion**      \~15× the injected volume
  **Foam density**        High-density structural grade (\~3 lbs/cu ft --- does not add meaningful load to soil)
  **Initial cure**        10--15 seconds (foam begins expanding immediately after injection)
  **90% strength**        \~30 minutes post-injection
  **Return to service**   Typically within 1 hour for light vehicles
  **Water resistance**    Closed-cell --- impermeable, will not erode or wash out like mudjacking slurry
  **Longevity**           Potentially the life of the concrete (20--50 years) if root cause is addressed
  **Good candidate**      Structurally sound slab with void beneath --- driveway, garage floor, pool deck, steps, interior slabs
  **Not a candidate**     Severely cracked or crumbling slab, active plumbing leak beneath, tree root heave

### **Poly vs. Mudjacking: The Key Differences**

Mudjacking is a legitimate alternative method for some applications. The
rep who can explain the difference accurately --- without dismissing
mudjacking wholesale --- earns credibility with customers who have
researched their options.

  **Hole size**            Poly: 5/8" (dime-sized) \| Mudjacking: 2"--2.5" (much more visible after patching)
  ------------------------ --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Material weight**      Poly: \~3 lbs/cu ft (adds no meaningful load) \| Mudjacking: 100+ lbs/cu ft (adds significant weight to already-stressed soil)
  **Erosion resistance**   Poly: closed-cell, does not erode \| Mudjacking: slurry can wash out over time, especially if drainage issue not corrected
  **Return to service**    Poly: \~1 hour \| Mudjacking: 24--48 hours
  **Patch visibility**     Poly: small holes, easier to patch nearly invisibly \| Mudjacking: larger holes, more obvious

### **In the Field: What to Say**

+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| **On the trip hazard / safety    |                                  |
| angle**                          |                                  |
|                                  |                                  |
| "What I documented today is a    |                                  |
| differential of \[X inches\] at  |                                  |
| that joint --- which is a        |                                  |
| recognized trip hazard. But the  |                                  |
| more important story is the void |                                  |
| beneath this panel, because that |                                  |
| void is what's going to continue |                                  |
| dropping the slab over the next  |                                  |
| few seasons. The injection fills |                                  |
| the void, restores the soil's    |                                  |
| support, and brings the slab     |                                  |
| back to grade. You'd have the    |                                  |
| surface back in service the same |                                  |
| day."                            |                                  |
+==================================+==================================+
|                                  | **⚠ AVOID:** Set the patch hole  |
|                                  | expectation before work begins.  |
|                                  | The 5/8" cement patches will be  |
|                                  | visible. They weather in over    |
|                                  | time but never completely        |
|                                  | disappear. Customers who aren't  |
|                                  | told this in advance will be     |
|                                  | disappointed by normal results.  |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+

**JOB TYPE 3**

**Structural Piers**
--------------------

Structural piers are steel shafts driven deep into the earth beneath a
settling foundation, bypassing the unstable near-surface soil and
transferring the weight of the home to load-bearing strata below. This
stabilizes the structure permanently and, in most cases, allows the
foundation to be hydraulically lifted back toward its original
elevation.

### **The Core Principle: Load Transfer**

The failing soil near the surface cannot support the home's weight.
Piers bypass that soil entirely, reaching down to a competent
load-bearing layer --- dense clay, gravel, or bedrock. Once the pier is
anchored in that layer, the home's weight travels down the steel shaft
and into material that has never moved and is unlikely to move.
Settlement stops because the load is no longer relying on the soil that
was failing.

### **Reading the Signs of Settlement**

  **Stair-step cracks (brick/block)**          Classic differential settlement --- the foundation has dropped at one corner relative to adjacent areas. The mortar joints are the weakest path and the crack follows them diagonally.
  -------------------------------------------- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Diagonal cracks at door/window corners**   The foundation is dropping differentially, racking the door frame out of square.
  **Vertical cracks in poured concrete**       Differential settlement pulling the wall apart. Width and displacement indicate severity.
  **Horizontal cracks in block walls**         LATERAL PRESSURE --- NOT settlement. Requires wall reinforcement evaluation. Never propose piers alone for horizontal cracking.
  **Cracks wider at top than bottom**          Foundation is rotating --- one end dropping relative to the other.
  **Sloping floors**                           1" per 8 feet: significant, warrants evaluation. 2"+ per 8 feet: urgent structural concern.
                                               **CRITICAL DIAGNOSTIC:** Horizontal cracks in a basement or crawl space wall indicate lateral soil pressure pushing the wall inward --- not settlement. This is a structural issue requiring wall reinforcement. A rep who recommends only drainage or only piers for a horizontally cracking wall is missing the structural problem.

### **Push Piers vs. Helical Piers**

  **Push piers --- how they work**      Hydraulically driven into the ground using the structure's own weight as resistance. Driven until refusal --- when the soil physically cannot be overcome --- confirming the pier has reached load-bearing depth.
  ------------------------------------- -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Push piers --- best for**           Heavy structures: poured concrete footings, masonry construction, two-story homes. The structure must be heavy enough to serve as the counterweight.
  **Push piers --- depth**              30--60+ feet to refusal, determined by where competent bearing is encountered.
  **Helical piers --- how they work**   Steel shaft with helical plates, mechanically screwed in by hydraulic torque motor. Capacity verified by correlating torque during installation to bearing capacity --- no structure weight required.
  **Helical piers --- best for**        Lighter structures, cracked or discontinuous footings, tight access areas, new construction. Also used when bedrock is too deep for push pier refusal.
  **Helical piers --- depth**           Typically 15--25 feet in Panhandle geology, driven to required torque value.

### **Honest Expectations to Set**

Stabilization is always the primary goal. Lift is what usually also
happens, and it is often significant --- but it is not guaranteed, and
the degree achievable depends on how long the settlement has been
occurring and what secondary damage exists in the structure above.
Cracks that are present before the repair will still be present
afterward. Wall cracks, drywall gaps, and separated trim typically
improve with lift but may need separate cosmetic repair. Set this
expectation before the crew arrives.

  -- -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
     **⚠ AVOID:** Never promise full restoration to original grade. The honest framing: 'Our primary goal is to stop the movement permanently and recover as much elevation as the structure will safely allow.'
  -- -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**JOB TYPE 4**

**Crawl Space Drainage**
------------------------

Crawl space drainage addresses bulk water --- liquid water physically
entering the crawl space from the water table, surface runoff, wall
seepage, or failed exterior drainage. This is a different problem from
vapor/humidity, which encapsulation addresses. The most important
diagnostic skill in crawl space moisture work is telling these two
apart.

### **Vapor vs. Bulk Water: The Critical Distinction**

  **Vapor indicators**        High relative humidity (\>60%), elevated wood moisture content (\>19%), condensation on surfaces, musty odor. No standing water visible.
  --------------------------- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Bulk water indicators**   Standing water visible on floor, water staining on foundation walls or piers, silt or mineral deposits at wall bases, efflorescence on block walls.
  **Vapor solution**          Encapsulation: vapor barrier, sealed vents, dehumidifier. A sump pump has zero effect on vapor.
  **Bulk water solution**     Interior perimeter drain and sump pump. Encapsulation alone cannot stop bulk water entry.
  **When both exist**         Drainage must be installed FIRST, then encapsulation. Installing the liner before drainage in an actively wet crawl space traps water beneath the liner.

### **Key System Components**

  **Perimeter drain**              4" perforated PVC or drain tile along interior perimeter at footing, sloped 1/8" per foot minimum toward sump
  -------------------------------- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Gravel bed + filter fabric**   Washed gravel surrounding pipe, non-woven geotextile wrap to prevent siltation
  **Sump basin**                   Perforated plastic basin at lowest point, minimum 18" deep, 18--24" diameter
  **Primary pump**                 Submersible, float-activated, 1/3--1/2 HP, 1,500--3,000+ GPH depending on water table
  **Battery backup**               12V deep-cycle marine battery. Replace every 3--5 years. Test annually. NON-OPTIONAL in this region.
  **Discharge endpoint**           Must discharge minimum 6 feet from foundation on a path that permanently drains away from the structure
  **Clean-out ports**              Every 10--20 feet; flush every 3--5 years
  **Encapsulation integration**    Liner tucked into/lapped over drain channel so wall seepage flows beneath liner to drain

### **In the Field: What to Say**

+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| **For the customer who already   |                                  |
| has a pump**                     |                                  |
|                                  |                                  |
| "Your pump is doing what it's    |                                  |
| supposed to do --- it's managing |                                  |
| water that physically reaches    |                                  |
| it. What we need is a perimeter  |                                  |
| channel that collects water from |                                  |
| all the entry points along the   |                                  |
| walls and routes all of it to    |                                  |
| the pump. Right now the pump is  |                                  |
| only serving the area            |                                  |
| immediately around it. The       |                                  |
| channel is what makes the system |                                  |
| complete."                       |                                  |
+==================================+==================================+
|                                  | **⚠ AVOID:** Battery backup is   |
|                                  | non-negotiable for this region.  |
|                                  | The most common scenario for     |
|                                  | crawl space flooding is a major  |
|                                  | storm --- exactly when you're    |
|                                  | most likely to lose power. A     |
|                                  | primary pump without backup      |
|                                  | leaves the system defenseless    |
|                                  | during the conditions it was     |
|                                  | installed to handle.             |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+

**JOB TYPE 5**

**Basement Drainage**
---------------------

Basement drainage addresses hydrostatic pressure --- the force exerted
by water-saturated soil against below-grade foundation walls and floor
slabs. Water weighs approximately 62 pounds per cubic foot. When soil
surrounding a basement becomes saturated, the accumulated weight of that
water mass pushes against every surface of the foundation wall and
increases by approximately 0.43 psi for every foot of depth below the
water table.

### **Why Surface Sealants Fail**

Concrete is porous at the microscopic level. Under significant
hydrostatic pressure, water is forced through the pores of otherwise
structurally sound concrete --- this is why basement walls 'sweat' even
without visible cracks. Interior masonry coatings work against
low-pressure dampness and capillary action, not against hydrostatic
pressure. Under sustained pressure, the coating's bond strength is
eventually exceeded and water works around or through it. Most coatings
fail within one to three wet seasons in high-pressure conditions. The
correct approach is pressure relief through interior drainage --- not
pressure resistance through sealants.

### **Where Water Enters**

  **Cove joint (most common)**        Where basement floor slab meets the foundation wall. Always has a slight gap. Hydrostatic pressure rising from below forces water up through this joint. Interior drainage specifically targets this entry point.
  ----------------------------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Wall pores**                      Hydrostatic pressure forcing water through pores of poured concrete or masonry. Shows as uniform wall dampness plus efflorescence (white mineral deposits) --- proof that water has been moving through the wall repeatedly.
  **Vertical/diagonal wall cracks**   Settlement or concrete shrinkage --- provides a direct path for pressurized water.
  **Horizontal wall cracks**          LATERAL SOIL PRESSURE --- NOT hydrostatic pressure alone. Requires wall reinforcement evaluation. Drainage alone does not address a structurally compromised wall.
  **Floor slab seepage**              When water table rises above basement floor level, hydrostatic pressure pushes water upward through the floor slab itself.
  **Window wells**                    Below-grade windows concentrate surface water. Inadequate well drainage allows water to accumulate and enter through frame or adjacent wall.

### **The Interior Drainage System**

  **Trench**                          12--18" wide saw-cut along interior perimeter at footing, exposing the footing-floor joint
  ----------------------------------- -----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Drain pipe**                      4" perforated PVC in washed gravel bed, sloped minimum 1/8" per foot toward sump
  **Wall gap/conduit**                Small gap left between new concrete and wall --- or wall conduit installed --- so wall seepage drains into channel rather than puddling on floor. Often skipped by less thorough contractors.
  **Floor restoration**               Trench refilled with concrete, finished flush with existing slab. The system is permanently below floor level and invisible when complete.
  **Sump basin + pump**               18--24" basin at lowest point of drain run, float-activated submersible pump, check valve on discharge line
  **Battery backup + sealed cover**   Battery backup for power outages. FEMA specifically recommends sealed sump covers to prevent soil gases from entering living space.

### **In the Field: What to Say**

+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+
| **To the customer who says       |                                  |
| they've painted the walls        |                                  |
| twice**                          |                                  |
|                                  |                                  |
| "Masonry coatings work against   |                                  |
| condensation and minor capillary |                                  |
| dampness --- not against         |                                  |
| hydrostatic pressure. When       |                                  |
| saturated soil is pushing water  |                                  |
| against your wall, that pressure |                                  |
| will eventually exceed any       |                                  |
| coating's bond strength and      |                                  |
| water works its way around or    |                                  |
| through. The drainage system     |                                  |
| doesn't try to stop the water at |                                  |
| the wall --- it gives the water  |                                  |
| a managed path before it builds  |                                  |
| that pressure. That's why it     |                                  |
| works long-term when coatings    |                                  |
| don't."                          |                                  |
+==================================+==================================+
|                                  | **ON EFFLORESCENCE:** The white  |
|                                  | chalky deposits on basement      |
|                                  | walls are not a cosmetic issue.  |
|                                  | They are physical proof that     |
|                                  | water has been moving through    |
|                                  | the wall repeatedly, carrying    |
|                                  | dissolved minerals and           |
|                                  | depositing them on the surface   |
|                                  | as it evaporates. A customer who |
|                                  | thinks they have 'some white     |
|                                  | stuff' actually has documented   |
|                                  | evidence of chronic water        |
|                                  | migration through their          |
|                                  | foundation wall.                 |
+----------------------------------+----------------------------------+

**PART 4**

**Objection Handling**
======================

An objection is not a rejection. It is a request for more --- more
information, more evidence, more reassurance, or more time to think. The
customer who objects is still in the conversation. The customer who says
nothing and leaves is the one you lost.

Every objection response should follow the same three-step structure:
acknowledge genuinely first (not "I understand, but..." --- the 'but'
erases the acknowledgment), diagnose before responding (ask what the
objection is really about before launching into content), then respond
with evidence rather than argument. Arguing correctly still produces
defensiveness. Evidence updates perception.

**The 16-Objection Quick Reference**
------------------------------------

The table below maps the most common objections to what they really
signal and the correct response approach. For complete response scripts,
see the Objection Handling reference deck.

  **Objection**                            **What It Really Means**                                                            **Response Approach**
  ---------------------------------------- ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- -----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  \"It\'s too expensive.\"                 Perceived value gap --- doesn't yet see why the repair is worth the cost.           Don't defend the price --- expand the value. Connect cost to what it prevents. Ask: 'Is it the total, or is it timing and cash flow?' Then present financing.
  \"I need to think about it.\"            Ambiguous --- could be undecided, needs spouse, comparing, or politely declining.   Ask the diagnostic question: 'What part are you still working through?' Then respond to that specific concern. Never leave without a specific agreed next step.
  \"Can you do it for less?\"              Testing whether the price was arbitrary and whether you'll cave.                    Hold the scope. Explain what each component does. Offer financing before reducing scope. If scope changes, document the trade-off explicitly.
  \"I want other quotes.\"                 Due diligence --- reasonable and legitimate.                                        Encourage it specifically. Give them a comparison checklist: pier type? battery backup? transferable warranty? Level the playing field.
  \"I\'ll wait and see.\"                  No clear cost to waiting --- urgency hasn't been made concrete.                     Use specific mechanism of progression: moisture threshold, settlement rate, hydrostatic pressure accumulation. Not 'these things get worse' --- the specific mechanism.
  \"Been like this for years.\"            Survivorship bias --- past stability misread as future stability.                   Validate the observation, then reframe with the progression curve: 'The home hasn't reached the threshold --- but the condition driving it hasn't changed.'
  \"Maybe next season.\"                   Timing deflection --- may or may not be a genuine constraint.                       Ask the diagnostic question: genuine constraint or decision anxiety? Offer a scheduling hold for real timing issues. Address the underlying concern for decision anxiety.
  \"Finances are tight right now.\"        Genuine constraint --- the most directly solvable timing objection.                 Present Upgrade and GoodLeap financing. Show the monthly payment, not the total. Five minutes, no obligation.
  \"I want a second opinion.\"             High-quality trust signal --- customer takes the issue seriously.                   Encourage it fully. Offer to share the inspection documentation with the engineer. Welcoming scrutiny is itself the most powerful credibility signal.
  \"I\'ve never heard of your company.\"   Request for proof of credibility and longevity.                                     Answer directly and confidently, then pull out the referral book. Local before-and-after photos from this community are the most powerful credibility evidence available.
  \"Neighbor said it wasn\'t serious.\"    Social trust conflict --- competing trusted source.                                 Don't argue the neighbor. Redirect to specific measurements: 'I'm telling you what I found in your home.' Let evidence create the new frame.
  \"Another company said it was fine.\"    Prior professional assessment as conflicting evidence.                              Ask what they specifically assessed. In most cases it was more general or addressed a different concern. Use the comparison to demonstrate today's specificity.
  \"Is this really necessary?\"            Direct credibility challenge --- wants evidence not assertion.                      Walk through each finding and connect every proposal line item to specific documented evidence. The evidence is the answer, not credentials.
  \"I read that \[alternative\] works.\"   Technical credibility challenge --- has done research.                              Engage with the specific thing they read. Acknowledge where it's valid, then explain why their specific conditions call for a different approach.
  \"Another company quoted less.\"         Scope visibility gap --- can't yet evaluate the difference.                         Ask for their scope. Compare component by component. Let the scope difference explain the price difference.
  \"Had it done before --- came back.\"    Burned customer --- trust threshold is at maximum.                                  Acknowledge the frustration genuinely and specifically first. Then ask what was installed. Explain the specific gap that produced the failure, and show how today's proposal closes it.

**PART 5**

**Key Numbers & Scripts**
=========================

This section collects the most important technical thresholds,
statistics, and model scripts from across the full curriculum into one
fast-reference page. Study these until they're in your head --- they are
the numbers and phrases that appear in the field most often.

**Critical Technical Thresholds**
---------------------------------

  **Normal wood moisture content**       12--15% (equilibrium in a dry environment)
  -------------------------------------- -----------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Elevated wood moisture**             19%+ (document, flag as risk zone)
  **Active rot threshold**               28%+ (wood-decay fungi can establish above this level)
  **Safe crawl space RH**                Below 60% (below 55% preferred; mold cannot sustain growth below 60%)
  **Daily soil vapor**                   10--15 gallons per day from exposed soil in a typical crawl space
  **Air exchange via stack effect**      40--50% of first-floor air comes from the crawl space below
  **Energy savings --- encapsulation**   15%+ reduction in annual HVAC costs typical
  **Floor slope --- significant**        1" differential per 8 feet warrants evaluation
  **Floor slope --- urgent**             2"+ differential per 8 feet: serious structural concern
  **Hydrostatic pressure weight**        Water weighs approximately 62 lbs/cu ft
  **Hydrostatic pressure increase**      Approximately 0.43 psi per foot of depth below water table
  **Poly foam expansion**                \~15× injected volume
  **Poly --- 90% strength**              \~30 minutes post-injection
  **Poly --- return to service**         \~1 hour for light vehicles
  **Poly hole size**                     5/8" (vs. 2"--2.5" for mudjacking)
  **Push pier depth range**              30--60+ feet to refusal
  **Helical pier depth range**           15--25 feet typical in this region
  **Sump drain slope**                   Minimum 1/8" per foot toward basin
  **Battery backup service**             Replace every 3--5 years; test annually
  **Discharge distance**                 Minimum 6 feet from foundation, sloped permanently away

**Key Statistics for Customer Conversations**
---------------------------------------------

  **Referral conversion rate**   Nielsen: referred customers convert at 4× the rate of cold leads
  ------------------------------ ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  **Referral LTV**               Wharton: referred customers have 25% higher lifetime value
  **Loss aversion ratio**        Behavioral economics: people feel the pain of a loss \~2× as strongly as an equivalent gain
  **Home value protection**      Interior drainage systems typically recoup 70--85% of cost in added home value and avoided repair expenses

**Model Scripts**
-----------------

### **Opening the Inspection Walk-Around**

  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  "Before I go underneath, I want to walk the perimeter with you for a few minutes --- I want to understand what you've observed and look at the exterior conditions that affect what happens below. The way water moves around this foundation tells a lot of the story."
  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **After Coming Out of the Crawl Space**

  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  "I've got a good picture of what's going on down there. Can we sit down for a few minutes? I'd like to walk you through the photos before we talk about what I'd recommend, because I think seeing it makes the recommendation make more sense."
  --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **Presenting Inspection Findings**

  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  "This is the moisture reading I took on your floor joists. This number is 24%. Normal is 12 to 15. Above 28%, wood-decay fungi can establish. You're already in a range where the conditions for damage are present. The same conditions that produced this reading will continue producing it every wet season --- this doesn't self-correct."
  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **Introducing Financing Before the Price**

  ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  "Before I show you the total, I want to mention that we have two financing options --- Upgrade and GoodLeap. A lot of our customers find that the monthly payment is significantly more manageable than the lump sum. I'll show you both scenarios."
  ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **The First Ask**

  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  "Based on everything I documented today and what we've gone through together, I'd like to get this scheduled for you. Can we find a date that works?"
  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **The Second Ask (after an objection is addressed)**

  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  "Given what I've explained about \[specific concern addressed\], does it make sense to move forward?"
  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **Asking for a Referral**

  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  "I really appreciate you saying that. If you know anyone else dealing with similar issues, I'd be grateful if you'd pass along my name --- I'd take good care of them."
  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### **The 5-Day Follow-Up Message**

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  "Hi \[Name\], I wanted to check in and see if you'd had a chance to think through what we discussed. I'm happy to answer any questions about the scope or talk through the financing options in more detail if that would help."
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Apex Foundation Specialists --- Florida Panhandle & South Alabama

Internal Training Use Only \| Not for Distribution
